  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ce117ab3-f2dd-406d-a334-bcc32a3aaf38'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1030330925332499713">Will Self has established himself as one of the most brilliant, daring, and inventive writers of his generation. <i>My Idea of Fun</i> is Will Self’s highly acclaimed first novel. The story of a devilishly clever international financier/marketing wizard and his young apprentice, <i>My Idea of Fun</i> is both a frighteningly dark subterranean exploration of capitalism run rampant and a w</span>
  <span id="freeText1030330925332499713" style="display:none">Will Self has established himself as one of the most brilliant, daring, and inventive writers of his generation. <i>My Idea of Fun</i> is Will Self’s highly acclaimed first novel. The story of a devilishly clever international financier/marketing wizard and his young apprentice, <i>My Idea of Fun</i> is both a frighteningly dark subterranean exploration of capitalism run rampant and a wickedly sharp, technically acute display of linguistic pyrotechnics that glows with pure white-hot brilliance. Ian Wharton is a very ordinary young man until he is taken under the wing of a gentleman known variously as Mr. Broadhurst, Samuel Northcliff, and finally and simply the Fat Controller. Loudmouthed, impeccably tailored, and a fount of bombastic erudition, the Fat Controller initiates Ian into the dark secrets of his arts -- of marketing, money, and the human psyche -- and takes Ian, and the reader, on a wild voyage around the edges of reality. As we careen into the twenty-first century, Self perfectly captures the zeitgeist of our times: money is the only common language; consumerism, violence, and psychosis (drug-induced and otherwise) prevail; and the human soul has become the ultimate product.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1030330925332499713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_87277001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87277001" />
    <a title="MJ Nicholls" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2386804-mj-nicholls"><img alt="MJ Nicholls" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374341850p2/2386804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87277001?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MJ Nicholls" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MJ Nicholls" href="/user/show/2386804-mj-nicholls">MJ Nicholls</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747582335" href="/book/show/1420738.My_Idea_Of_Fun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2386804-mj-nicholls?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2386804-mj-nicholls?shelf=sassysassenachs">sassysassenachs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87277001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18190084037542387044">We asked three pupils of Roswell High Class 2B what was their idea of fun:<br/><br/><i>Daniel sez: </i><br/><br/>“I want to be the delete button on a keyboard. If I was the delete button on a keyboard I would backspace the novels of Iain Banks and Nicole Krauss and I would delete mummy’s divorce papers. But fantasies aside, what I do for fun is I fill balloons to bursting point with custard then drop them on the heads of teachers after school. I have the power to dematerialise at will so they never find out who slathered </span>
  <span id="freeText18190084037542387044" style="display:none">We asked three pupils of Roswell High Class 2B what was their idea of fun:<br /><br /><i>Daniel sez: </i><br /><br />“I want to be the delete button on a keyboard. If I was the delete button on a keyboard I would backspace the novels of Iain Banks and Nicole Krauss and I would delete mummy’s divorce papers. But fantasies aside, what I do for fun is I fill balloons to bursting point with custard then drop them on the heads of teachers after school. I have the power to dematerialise at will so they never find out who slathered them in yellow goo. Ha!”<br /><br /><i>Phil sez: </i><br /><br />“My idea of fun is to go up to girls and kick them in the shins again and again until the blood oozes out their legs. Then I lick it up and lick the back of a stamp and I say: ‘Your head’s bleeding Your Majesty!’ After that I go to the pond and have a nice sit down while the cygnets carry me aloft to their secret poker den where I play crabs for chocolate coins and whip some swan ass. Later on I like to watch re-runs of <i>The Norm Show</i>.”<br /><br /><i>Nicola sez: </i><br /><br />“I think it would be fun to put the Prime Minister David Cameron on a blimp bound for Qatar and make him start a new life there among the Qataris, eating boiled rabbit and porkscrews. Later on I think it would be fun to represent Niger in the African Song Contest. The singer could come on and attempt to make an audible vocalisation before collapsing onstage from the kind of food deprivation that makes every action we ever do in the West look like pissing against a giant tree day in day out, forever and ever. I also like darts.”<br /><br />*<br /><br />HAVEN’T READ THIS FOR WHILE. IT’S GOOD. <br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1032194899" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1032194899" />
    <a title="Anthony Vacca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27183668-anthony-vacca"><img alt="Anthony Vacca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604067844p2/27183668.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1032194899?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Vacca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Vacca" href="/user/show/27183668-anthony-vacca">Anthony Vacca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780679750932" href="/book/show/119108.My_Idea_of_Fun">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032194899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer395028449282067428">Will Self's first proper novel is about as rude, unruly, and raucously loquacious as one would come to expect from the writer who likes to decorate every page with trinkets of unfamiliar locution, who has a penchant for endless slithers of alliteration, who will take the time to describe the hairs in a hobo's nose with great detail and zest, and who will shock your puritan sensibilities by inexplicably growing a vagina at the back of a character's knee or giving a game account of acts of decapit</span>
  <span id="freeText395028449282067428" style="display:none">Will Self's first proper novel is about as rude, unruly, and raucously loquacious as one would come to expect from the writer who likes to decorate every page with trinkets of unfamiliar locution, who has a penchant for endless slithers of alliteration, who will take the time to describe the hairs in a hobo's nose with great detail and zest, and who will shock your puritan sensibilities by inexplicably growing a vagina at the back of a character's knee or giving a game account of acts of decapitation and necrophilia.<br /><br />That last bit is the part-time narrator of <i>My Idea of Fun</i>'s idea of fun. Ian is a plump momma's boy with a gift of photographic memory that is more akin to virtual reality or astral projection. A demonic wizard - the massive and terrifying entity known as The Fat Controller - takes young Ian under his wing and shows him the powers of cruelty, alchemy, and market manipulation. As Ian grows older and becomes a yuppie-ish accountant, he must come to a reckoning with The Fat Controller and his own fragile feelings of morality. This pitched confrontation crosses over into a nightmarish dream world, courtesy of the new-age techniques of a psychiatrist of dubious ethics and methods, the big-bearded Dr. Gyggle.<br /><br />That is kind of a description of this book's plot, but really the narrative format serves best as a vehicle for Self's increasingly confident prose, his bleak, black humor, his unflinching commitment to his grotesque satirical view of the world, and his batshit insane imagination. <br /><br />Me? My idea of fun is reading <i>My Idea of Fun</i>, natch! </span>
  <a data-text-id="395028449282067428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34000446" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34000446" />
    <a title="Caterina Fake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570719-caterina-fake"><img alt="Caterina Fake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422987880p2/1570719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34000446?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caterina Fake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caterina Fake" href="/user/show/1570719-caterina-fake">Caterina Fake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570719-caterina-fake?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570719-caterina-fake?shelf=wrote-a-review">wrote-a-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34000446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2471788732119512823">A truly ghastly experience, My Idea of Fun records the memories, justifications and sheer relish of a delusional maniac, serial killer, animal torturer and all around repulsive fellow, couched in prose so purple it's no longer a part of the visible spectrum. As the protagonist's predilections are presented on the first page, you can't say you didn't know what you were getting into. Against the chidings of my conscience I continued reading, fascinated, much as you can't not look at a grisly autom</span>
  <span id="freeText2471788732119512823" style="display:none">A truly ghastly experience, My Idea of Fun records the memories, justifications and sheer relish of a delusional maniac, serial killer, animal torturer and all around repulsive fellow, couched in prose so purple it's no longer a part of the visible spectrum. As the protagonist's predilections are presented on the first page, you can't say you didn't know what you were getting into. Against the chidings of my conscience I continued reading, fascinated, much as you can't not look at a grisly automobile accident as you wheel by on the highway. You can't help but admire Self's turn of phrase, his dictionary squeezings, his calculated yet slick deployments of rib-cracking funniness, but you nonetheless wish he weren't quite so sick. The book is a compelling enough read. There are a couple flubbed hallucinatory sequences of a William Burroughs variety which I flat out skipped. I frankly didn't give a brown M &amp; M about our protagonist's career in advertising or his (possibly meant to be loathsome?) yuppiedom. Self fell asleep on the job more than a few times, misplacing his character's characteristics, straining and failing to shock, including flat or pointless scenes. Only the scenes in which The Fat Controller played a part were gripping, though inevitably gripping a part of you you'd rather had never been gripped at all. By the end I was just turning pages and feeling icky. That the editors or the author were feeling somewhat insecure about whether or not this book was to be taken as satire is evidenced by the book's anxious subtitle A Cautionary Tale. Wash yourself thoroughly after reading this one, though that may not suffice. A colonic might be more appropriate. For the very susceptible, an exorcism. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2471788732119512823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2541565751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6951876236139987730">The best way I can describe or categorize this book is by saying it's magical realism with the magic being of the nightmarish type. A very black comedy of sorts, it wildly strays between consciousness and unconsciousness in the vaguely linear life of Ian Wharton. It will confuse you and probably anger you but Will Self's sharp intellect and manic wisdom is undeniable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140234008" href="/book/show/929429.My_Idea_of_Fun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/454255-velvetink?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/454255-velvetink?shelf=sf-fantasy">sf-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/454255-velvetink?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128767879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11778880244361089021">In a way you have to take this as a kind of fantasy. Ian Wharton could have any number of variations of mental illness and The Fat Controller could be an hallucination or could indeed be The Devil. <br/><br/>You are sad for this boy Ian as he grows up, painfully awkward without a father and pity him his social climbing but distant mother and wonder where his relationship with The Fat Controller aka (Mr. Broadhurst/Samuel Northcliffe) is going. <br/><br/>You wonder a lot about The Fat Controller too and Ian's Eideti</span>
  <span id="freeText11778880244361089021" style="display:none">In a way you have to take this as a kind of fantasy. Ian Wharton could have any number of variations of mental illness and The Fat Controller could be an hallucination or could indeed be The Devil. <br /><br />You are sad for this boy Ian as he grows up, painfully awkward without a father and pity him his social climbing but distant mother and wonder where his relationship with The Fat Controller aka (Mr. Broadhurst/Samuel Northcliffe) is going. <br /><br />You wonder a lot about The Fat Controller too and Ian's Eidetic memory and whether there is magic involved or whether Ian is in fact an idiot savant of some kind.... I was disappointed Will Self didn't take the eidetic memory idea to another level but I guess that's the non-fiction fan in me. Will Self's choice of words can take your breath away with their aptness and so do the few truly violent passages that appear. One is never really sure if they in fact happened in Ian's real life or in his imaginative headspace. His forays into a medical cure by Deep Sleep prove nightmareish when he arrives in The Land of Children's Jokes. The characters get crazy with fabulous descriptive passages verging on the psychadelic until you begin to lose the plot a bit. And the plot is that you the reader make a judgement, Will Self likes audience participation and at the end you get to make up your own mind.<br /><br />There are some seriously funny parts and some violent instances that shock you like when you have first been slapped on the face &amp; wonder what hit you. It's an awakening experience. <br /><br />Not the kind of book I could read a lot of normally but it totally distracted me from the horrors of my own life while I was reading it ~ and that is probably my idea of fun at the moment..... <br />_______________________________________________________________________ <br /><br />Seems quite a few people objected strongly to this book. Granted it's strange so far...but not yet shocking. I like Will Self's writing and this is no exception. What's interesting is how the main character has an Eidetic memory and what he does with it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11778880244361089021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1435159658122707803">My favorite Bildungsroman ever, 'My Idea of Fun' is a sort of 'Great Expectations' for the crack generation. 'My Idea of Fun' is ostensibly about Ian, and his life as a tool of the Fat Controller. However, everything in this book is deeply metaphorical. Like the more psychedelic works of late-period Burroughs and Alan Gullette, the book is best read sideways, allowing the scenes that are created to first manifest before attempting to decrypt their true meaning. This is mind-bending stuff, and no</span>
  <span id="freeText1435159658122707803" style="display:none">My favorite Bildungsroman ever, 'My Idea of Fun' is a sort of 'Great Expectations' for the crack generation. 'My Idea of Fun' is ostensibly about Ian, and his life as a tool of the Fat Controller. However, everything in this book is deeply metaphorical. Like the more psychedelic works of late-period Burroughs and Alan Gullette, the book is best read sideways, allowing the scenes that are created to first manifest before attempting to decrypt their true meaning. This is mind-bending stuff, and not for the faint of heart.</span>

<div id="review_650675644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/650675644" />
    <a title="Leo Robertson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7619789-leo-robertson"><img alt="Leo Robertson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571602096p2/7619789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/650675644?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leo Robertson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leo Robertson" href="/user/show/7619789-leo-robertson">Leo Robertson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer650675644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1593660668932786006">Soooo when I’m reading a book, I’ll sit with a flashcard and write down all the new words/words I didn’t know had different forms/ words it would not occur to me to write, and then I upload the words to <a href='http://ankisrs.net/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anki</a> so that I can test myself on them and hopefully memorise them. I’ve been doing this for about a year and have racked up nearly 1100 words that I wouldn’t otherwise use! From the near-uselessness of reglet or machicolation to the newly essential magniloquence, prolixity, experiential, or stea</span>
  <span id="freeText1593660668932786006" style="display:none">Soooo when I’m reading a book, I’ll sit with a flashcard and write down all the new words/words I didn’t know had different forms/ words it would not occur to me to write, and then I upload the words to <a href="http://ankisrs.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">Anki</a> so that I can test myself on them and hopefully memorise them. I’ve been doing this for about a year and have racked up nearly 1100 words that I wouldn’t otherwise use! From the near-uselessness of reglet or machicolation to the newly essential magniloquence, prolixity, experiential, or steatopygic. If you perform this exercise, no matter what your enjoyment of a book, no reading is ever truly wasted. And you rarely get through a Will Self novel without a new word or two- ha! so what happened should not have surprised me too much, but check this out:<br><br> <span>[image error]</span><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>(In some of these you can see my sparkly toenails. You’re welcome!)<br>[Goddamn image errors! Ahhh I'll fix it later...]<br><br>I filled one of those cards by about pg 200/278, which was incidentally around the point that the book stopped making any sense. I would have filled two maybe three cards if me and Will hadn’t been collecting the same words all this time. But I dunno… I feel like what I have picked apart here is the secret contents of a little notebook of words that Will kept on his writing desk, cynically ticking off each one as he put them in this story, and this kind of lexicographical clinicality cannot help but extirpate the ultimate murated form- oh sorry were you not keeping up with me and Will? I mean it takes you out of the story. There there, you’re not as clever as me and him, it’s okay, you’re only anyone, it happens.<br><br>Yeah but because I’ve been collecting so many words from so many different books for so long, and still managed to find so many new ones, seems like evidence to me that Will was trying super hard to be obfuscatory. Why would he do that? Because he wanted to prove he was clever. Why would he want to prove he was clever? Because he was scared. Why was he scared? First novel, they’re pretty much always not so great (unless we’re talking about The God of Small Things of course, because in that case the book was pure horseshit!)<br><br>But hey! Great writers are the ones that kept going. And Self went on to write The Book of Dave, Tough Tough Toys for Tough Tough Boys, Umbrella, and the first half of How The Dead Live!<br><br>I don’t know if the story was any good, I was too distracted. And I’m gonna give you the list of words, so I wouldn’t recommend reading this novel given that the list of words is all I took from it :S<br>I read that a DJ can become competitive if he keeps an excel sheet cataloguing the BPM of different songs in different musical genres (probably some program does this for them nowadays), so as a writer’s equivalent, you can’t see my 1100 words- but you probably knew more of them than me anyways :D I don’t see any harm in at least sharing Will’s Fun list though- not necessarily words I didn’t know, but also those it doesn’t occur to me to normally use :)<br><br>(Well these 5 are from Inherent Vice:<br>Copacetic<br>Praetorian<br>Tessitura<br>Yucca<br>Vig)<br><br>And now- and I should say, a handful of repeats, a few I’m pretty sure I already have in my Anki pack and a number that I’m not sure if I read correctly from the card, but I definitely do not remember the context:<br><br>Embrasure<br>Sylph-hood<br>Conciliatory<br>Furbelow<br>Fluting<br>Macrame<br>Patina<br>Deja entendu<br>Hinterland<br>Shambolic<br>Djellaba<br>Chitties<br>Piltjurri<br>Pelf<br>Lapidary<br>Shofar<br>Obeisance<br>Gallimaufry <br>Peccadillo<br>Demiurge<br>Furfend<br>Betoken<br>Panatella<br>Hypnogogia<br>Obdurate<br>Basso<br>Undulant<br>Hittites<br>Autohagiography<br>Moue<br>Concertina<br>Vermiculation<br>Homunculus<br>Stogies<br>Perforce<br>Peregrination<br>Sanatorial<br>Stupa<br>Groyne<br>Ichor<br>Ruckle<br>Shanghail<br>Agadir<br>Conveyance<br>Consanguinity<br>Sprog<br>Eidetiker<br>Scrungy<br>Vestigial<br>Stentorian<br>Spindrift<br>Cogitation<br>Crepitation<br>Adumbrate<br>Micturation<br>Mondial<br>Substratum<br>Bedizened<br>Numinous<br>Costermongering<br>Ambit<br>Prelate<br>Rosicrucian<br>Mutable<br>Alembic<br>Aludel<br>Athenor<br>Caduceus<br>Hypostatical<br>Prestidigitation<br>Capacious<br>Scryer<br>Tetragrammation<br>Thaumaturgical<br>Avoirdupois<br>Peregrination<br>Sanatorial<br>Chattel<br>Insouciance<br>Billet(s)-doux<br>Applique<br>Bibelots<br>Baize<br>Derogated<br>Roc<br>Souk<br>Assertorics<br>Kapok<br>Eminence <div id="review_395463270" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/395463270" />
    <a title="Graham Hughes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12018532-graham-hughes"><img alt="Graham Hughes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465420405p2/12018532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/395463270?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graham Hughes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graham Hughes" href="/user/show/12018532-graham-hughes">Graham Hughes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer395463270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13926077707451878512">Some reviewers have slated this book for being so disgusting, sickening, gross, and so on. Do they assume that all writing is intended to be an endorsement of its subject matter? Will Self simply created these depraved characters and made a story out of them. We don't have to <i>like</i> these people in order to be gripped by the story, which I certainly was.<br/><br/>It isn't easy reading, and can be deeply uncomfortable at times, but it's well worth the effort. And, this man has an incredible way with words.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_332606603" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332606603" />
    <a title="Kai Manne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9625886-kai-manne"><img alt="Kai Manne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338646735p2/9625886.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/332606603?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai Manne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai Manne" href="/user/show/9625886-kai-manne">Kai Manne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer332606603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7601642141996155361">I've been prompted to write a review for this by the number of 1 star reviews I have seen.<br/><br/>This is one of my favourite books ever. However, before you read this book there are a number of provisos to consider. There are things that I believe about literature. Also note, not all of these may apply directly to this particular book, as I would be giving away too much if they did. Finally, the provisos will sit under a spoiler alert at the end of the review, but are intended to be read at this point.</span>
  <span id="freeText7601642141996155361" style="display:none">I've been prompted to write a review for this by the number of 1 star reviews I have seen.<br /><br />This is one of my favourite books ever. However, before you read this book there are a number of provisos to consider. There are things that I believe about literature. Also note, not all of these may apply directly to this particular book, as I would be giving away too much if they did. Finally, the provisos will sit under a spoiler alert at the end of the review, but are intended to be read at this point. I suspect (and having read many of the reviews before I got bored this suspicion is based on some evidence) that many of the one star reviews were due to people disagreeing with many of the provisos, particularly numbers 1 and 2. <br /><br />Having considered the provisos, and whether this may or may not be the novel for you I shall proceed.<br /><br />This book made me feel ill. This book made me laugh. This book is also exceptionally well written. There are few modern authors I enjoy reading who can match Self's prose when he is in form. This book made me think deeply about a large variety of issues in our society. Reading this book was My Idea of Fun. If you don't mind being made to feel uncomfortable, and are prepared to buckle in for the ride, it may be your idea of fun too. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />1) Sometimes it is a good thing to be made to feel uncomfortable. Not all literature is meant to feel good and uplifting. We have evolved to have a number of different emotions, for different purposes, and good literature can explore all of these.<br /><br />2) You don't have to like the characters in a book for the book to be a good book. <br /><br />3) You don't have to know if the events occurring in a book are real or fantasy. I love books that explore the lines between psychosis and reality, between psychosis and magic, between fantasy and reality, and there's nothing wrong with the unreliable narrator.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="7601642141996155361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_709193937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/709193937" />
    <a title="Lee Battersby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1101417-lee-battersby"><img alt="Lee Battersby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471081642p2/1101417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/709193937?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee Battersby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee Battersby" href="/user/show/1101417-lee-battersby">Lee Battersby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer709193937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9012081548239148793">Smug, self-satisfied, pretentious twaddle from a cutting-edge writer fearlessly treading unspoiled ground covered twenty years previously by the likes of Robert Bloch and Joyce Carol Oates. Between the high-handed purple prose; long winding passages saying nothing really but jammed in for the sole purpose of demonstrating the breadth of Self's vocabulary; and a plot so minor it might have filled a Richard Matheson short story on a bad day, this is a Jericho's trumpet of nothingness. Tedious and </span>
  <span id="freeText9012081548239148793" style="display:none">Smug, self-satisfied, pretentious twaddle from a cutting-edge writer fearlessly treading unspoiled ground covered twenty years previously by the likes of Robert Bloch and Joyce Carol Oates. Between the high-handed purple prose; long winding passages saying nothing really but jammed in for the sole purpose of demonstrating the breadth of Self's vocabulary; and a plot so minor it might have filled a Richard Matheson short story on a bad day, this is a Jericho's trumpet of nothingness. Tedious and frustrating in equal measure, even the gleeful shock value of Self's "Oh, I'm so naughty" moments come across as little more than a small boy jumping in puddles to upset his parents. Tiresome. DNF.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9012081548239148793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_227776485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227776485" />
    <a title="Justin Evans" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2184529-justin-evans"><img alt="Justin Evans" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319658063p2/2184529.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227776485?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin Evans" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin Evans" href="/user/show/2184529-justin-evans">Justin Evans</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2184529-justin-evans?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227776485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5715734243894116815">What does it say about me that I didn't find this book very shocking? For all but twenty pages, it's a satire on metaphysical bildungsromans (romanen?) and a pretty withering criticism of contemporary society. Okay, so far so good. Plenty of people got there first, it's true: revoltingly fat man as a figure of Satan? McCarthy in Blood Meridian beat him by 5 years. Links between repulsive violence and the less productive aspects of capitalist society? Ever heard of American Psycho, Will? Even the</span>
  <span id="freeText5715734243894116815" style="display:none">What does it say about me that I didn't find this book very shocking? For all but twenty pages, it's a satire on metaphysical bildungsromans (romanen?) and a pretty withering criticism of contemporary society. Okay, so far so good. Plenty of people got there first, it's true: revoltingly fat man as a figure of Satan? McCarthy in Blood Meridian beat him by 5 years. Links between repulsive violence and the less productive aspects of capitalist society? Ever heard of American Psycho, Will? Even the supposedly shocking bits are a bit rehashed- getting it off inside gory wounds? Ballard, Crash. <br />So the 'shock' isn't very shocking, unless you've only been reading novels by Martin Amis and A. S. Byatt for the last 40 years, which is apparently true of the British cognoscenti. <br />Otherwise? Well, the problem is that Self is very good at the shocking gore stuff, but there isn't much of it and what there is has been, as I said, rehashed.* He's not so good at making his own criticisms of society coherent. Obviously he thinks shit is fucked up and shit, but that's about as much depth as I can find. He hints at the problems of reification and alienation (actual alienation, not teenager-wearing-black-sitting-in-his-room-can't-connect-to-society alienation), but maybe I'm just reading that into it? <br />Otherwise, the plot twist is a little tiresome (although this time he got in *before* Palahniuk, so that's one for the Brits) and kind of obvious, and there's so much pointless sub-surrealist garbage in the second half that I really started to question if he had any idea what he was doing at all. <br /><br />On the upside, splendidly written and mean enough that I'd be willing to try his other books. But don't go looking for shock, plot or character here. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />* Spoiler alert: I confess the whole 'sucking the severed penis of a tortured, dead dog' thing was unexpected. But imagine how much more 'shocking' it would have been if the dog had been alive. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5715734243894116815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1200980301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200980301" />
    <a title="Tom Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31467977-tom-quinn"><img alt="Tom Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574458226p2/31467977.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1200980301?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Quinn" href="/user/show/31467977-tom-quinn">Tom Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1200980301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11290264337090858913">Stop me if you've heard this one:<br/><br/>A magician moves into a trailer park. He befriends an awkward prepubescent kid, guides him through adolescence, teaches him some mystical rites, and takes him on as an apprentice. Later it turns out that he might be the devil (or, as he'd probably prefer you to put it, The Devil). The kid goes into marketing and into therapy to forget about his supernatural dalliances, but the pact he made with his instructor looms heavily over his head. It's two parts <i>Doctor Fau</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11290264337090858913" style="display:none">Stop me if you've heard this one:<br /><br />A magician moves into a trailer park. He befriends an awkward prepubescent kid, guides him through adolescence, teaches him some mystical rites, and takes him on as an apprentice. Later it turns out that he might be the devil (or, as he'd probably prefer you to put it, The Devil). The kid goes into marketing and into therapy to forget about his supernatural dalliances, but the pact he made with his instructor looms heavily over his head. It's two parts <i>Doctor Faustus</i>, one part <i>Great Expectations</i>, and a liberal sprinkling of <i>American Psycho</i>.<br /><br />2.5 stars out of 5. I forgave it its slow start because once it's worked up a good head of steam this one really takes off, but then it sputters and stalls out again midway through. It is uneven with several laggy spots throughout (most frequently when the supernatural stuff takes back burner to a more standard <i>bildungsroman</i>) and it really loses focus towards the ending. Some have complained about the overblown vocabulary and pompous "purple prose" but honestly that was my favorite part. The sections where this all works are really enjoyable, but it's not consistent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11290264337090858913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1335784561" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1335784561" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1335784561?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dustin Long" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dustin Long" href="/user/show/317279-dustin-long">Dustin Long</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1335784561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2399652418750841346">Even in a work as early as this, Self is clearly a very talented writer. The sentences alone are enough to get this book a two star review. I also liked the way the book explored the limitations of different psychological/psychiatric models as explanations for the main character's experiences. I didn't really feel that the over the top violence (really only in a few sections) was justified, though, and the ending was a little cheap with the sudden shift in point of view. Maybe it was coming to t</span>
  <span id="freeText2399652418750841346" style="display:none">Even in a work as early as this, Self is clearly a very talented writer. The sentences alone are enough to get this book a two star review. I also liked the way the book explored the limitations of different psychological/psychiatric models as explanations for the main character's experiences. I didn't really feel that the over the top violence (really only in a few sections) was justified, though, and the ending was a little cheap with the sudden shift in point of view. Maybe it was coming to this after reading Umbrella, which I absolutely loved, but this one was slightly disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2399652418750841346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('veuUmJib6sPYvP39PoaCRFy5bM74xzMrrnGpdVxW1M3uCHLIGdX9DwLFw787boBLOKCb9chp5cbVUPHtknVZaA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yqpa3ZFoXSnCbrRQJTMSLoUupCxJMc6utSpUOnBGJYWZSbyNECZK5RgXihIg2xAh4TdTF3mfGEPOCwyivmWoIA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Now, in his most topical and visceral novel yet, he ushers us into the consciousness of two men in the shadow of a bloodbath: Gretch Gravey, a cryptic psychopath with a small army of burnout followers, and E. N. Flood, the troubled police detective tasked with unpacking and understanding his mind.\n\nA mingled simulacrum of Charles Manson, David Koresh, and Thomas Harris’s Buffalo Bill, Gravey is a sinister yet alluring God figure who enlists young metal head followers to kidnap neighboring women and bring them to his house—where he murders them and buries their bodies in a basement crypt. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10058519878083447242">William Self is an English novelist, reviewer and columnist. He received his education at University College School, Christ's College Finchley, and Exeter College, Oxford. He is married to journalist Deborah Orr.<br/><br/>Self is known for his satirical, grotesque and fantastic novels and short stories set in seemingly parallel universes.<br/></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/trivia/work/114670-my-idea-of-fun">Trivia About My Idea of Fun</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
        <div class="mediumText">
          1 trivia question
          <br />
          
        </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right;" href="/trivia/work/114670-my-idea-of-fun">More quizzes &amp; trivia...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>


      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/114670-my-idea-of-fun">Quotes from My Idea of Fun</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;We're like coke heads or chronic masturbators, aren't we? Attempting to crank the last iota of abandonment out of an instrinsically empty and mechanical experience. We push the plunger home, we abrade the clitoris, we yank the penis and we feel nothing. Not exactly nothing, worse than nothing, we feel a flicker or a prickle, the sensual equivalent of a retinal after-image. That's our fun now, not fun itself, only a tired allusion to it. Nevertheless, we feel certain that if we can allude to fun one more time, make a firm statement about it, it will return like the birds after winter.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/6572540-we-re-like-coke-heads-or-chronic-masturbators-aren-t-we-attempting">9 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;How can it be so, this hovering sense of being both victim and perpetrator, both us and them, both me and him? Have we been expelled from an arcadia of fun where nature provided us with innocent automata, lowing and braying machines for our amusement?<br /><br />I doubt it. I doubt it very much. I tell you what I think, since you ask, since you dare to push your repulsive face at me, from out of the smooth paintwork of my heavily mortgaged heart. I think there was only so much fun to go round, only so much and no more available. We've used it all up country dancing in the gloaming, kissing by moonlight, eating shellfish while the sun shatters on our upturned fork and we make the <i>bon point</i>. And of course, the think about fun is that it exists solely in retrospect, in retroscendence; when you're having fun you are perforce abandoned, unthinking. Didn't we have fun, well, didn't we? You know we did.<br /><br />You're with me now, aren't you? We're leaving the party together. We pause on the stairs and although we left of our own accord, pulled our coat from under the couple entwined on the bed, we already sense that it was the wrong decision, that there was a hidden hand pushing us out, wanting to exclude us.<br /><br />We pause on the stairs and we hear the party going on without us, a shrill of laughter, a skirl of music. Is it too late to go back? Will we feel silly if we go back up and announce to no one in particular, 'Look, the cab hasn't arrived. We thought we'd just come back up and wait for it, have a little more fun.'<br /><br />Well, yes, yes, we will feel silly, bloody silly, because it isn't true. The cab has arrived, we can see it at the bottom of the stairs, grunting in anticipation, straining to be clutched and directed, to take us away. Away from fun and home, home to the suburbs of maturity.<br /><br />One last thing. You never thought that being grown up would mean having to be quite so - how can I put it? Quite so - grown up. Now did you? You didn't think that you'd have to work at it quite so hard. It's so relentless, this being grown up, this having to be considered, poised, at home with a shifting four-dimensional matrix of Entirely Valid Considerations. You'd like to get a little tiddly, wouldn't you? You'd like to fiddle with the buttons of reality as he does, feel it up without remorse, without the sense that you have betrayed some shadowy commitment.<br /><br />Don't bother. I've bothered. I've gone looking for the child inside myself. Ian, the Startrite kid. I've pursued him down the disappearing paths of my own psyche. I am he as he is me, as we are all . . . His back, broad as a standing stone . . . My footsteps, ringing eerily inside my own head. I'm turning in to face myself, and face myself, and face myself. I'm looking deep into my own eyes. Ian, is that you, my significant other? I can see you now for what you are, Ian Wharton. You're standing on a high cliff, chopped off and adumbrated by the heaving green of the sea. You're standing hunched up with the dull awareness of the hard graft. The heavy workload that is life, that is death, that is life again, everlasting, world without end.<br /><br />And now, Ian Wharton, now that you are no longer the subject of this cautionary tale, merely its object, now that you are just another unproductive atom staring out from the windows of a branded monad, now that I've got you where I want you, let the wild rumpus begin.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/10485710-how-can-it-be-so-this-hovering-sense-of-being">0 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/114670-my-idea-of-fun">More quotes&hellip;</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
